Objection from Infinite Numbers and Its Answer
Jurjani presents the objection from infinite numbers and answers it by distinguishing actual and potential infinity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection from infinite numbers to the burhan al-tatbiq and how the answer distinguishes between actual and potential infinity.

Core Idea
The burhan al-tatbiq only applies to things with actual existence, not to potential infinities like numbers.

In this passage, Jurjani presents a sophisticated objection to the burhan al-tatbiq based on infinite numbers. The objector argues that the proof would apply to two infinite series of numbers, leading to a contradiction, yet numbers are accepted as infinite. Jurjani answers by carefully distinguishing between actual infinity (where individuals have existed) and potential infinity (where they have not yet occurred). This distinction is crucial for defending the proof against such objections.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Understand the objector's claim: the burhan al-tatbiq seems to apply to infinite number series, yet numbers are infinite. Note the example of doubling 1 and doubling 1000 infinitely.
The objector is trying to show a counterexample to the proof.
2
Identify the answer's core distinction
The answer revolves around the difference between what 'existence has determined' (past events that actually occurred) and what it has not (future events). For the past, alignment is realistic; for the future, it is hypothetical.
This distinction blocks the objection.
3
Understand 'hypothetical existence'
The answer explains that for future numbers, the assumption of alignment is impossible because the individuals do not exist yet. Assuming alignment yields only a hypothetical contradiction that does not prove impossibility in reality.
This is a key nuance in kalam reasoning.
4
Learn the technical meaning of naqd
The passage defines naqd as a proof applying to something but the judgment not following. The proper response is either to deny the proof's applicability or to deny the absence of the judgment.
This definition frames the entire discussion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وقد نقض ) هذا الدليل ( بمراتب الأعداد لأن الدليل قائم فيها مع عدم تناهيها)، وذلك لأنا نفرض جملتين من الأعداد إحداهما تضعيف الواحد مراراً غير متناهية، والأخرى تضعيف الألف كذلك، ثم نطبق إحداهما على الأخرى بأن نضع الأول من الزائدة بإزاء الأول من الناقصة ونسرد الكلام إلى آخره، مع أن هاتين الجملتين غير متناهيتين بالضرورة. (والجواب ) عن هذا النقض ( أن المعلولات)، بل عن قوله : (لأنا نفرض إلخ المطابق لما سبق أن يقول : كما في شرح المقاصد بأن يفرض جملتان إحداهما من الواحد والثانية مما فوقه بمتناه ونطبق إحداهما بالأخرى إلخ والشارح قدس سره حمل مؤونة تضعيف الواحد وتضعيف ما فوقه مراراً غير متناهية ليحصل الجملتان المتباينتان ويكون جريان التطبيق فيهما أظهر مما فرض سابقاً من تطبيق آحاد الجزء بآحاد الكل فإن قلت : فيما سبق كان تطبيق الواحد بالواحد وفي صورة النقض على كلا التقديرين تطبيق الواحد بالكثير قلت : هذا الفرق لا يجدي نفعاً لأن في كل منهما تطبيق المتناهي بالمتناهي، فإن استلزم خلاف المفروض في الأول استلزم خلاف المفروض في الثاني وإلا فلا ثم اعلم أن جريان البرهان في الأعداد ليس باعتبار لاتناهيها بالفعل إذ لا يقول به أحد من المتكلمين لأن المعدودات متناهية خارجاً وذهناً والتصور التفصيلي لها ممتنع من القوى القاصرة والإجمالي لا تعدد فيه فضلاً اللاتناهي وفي علمه تعالى متناهية ضرورة إحاطة العلم بها وكذا في علم المبادي العالية إن قلنا بوجودها والعلم التفصيلي لها بما لا يتناهى بل جريانه فيها باعتبار عدم تناهيها بالقوة باعتبار وجودها في المعدودات الخارجة الغير المتناهية في الاستقبال ومنشؤه عدم الفرق بين وجود الأمور المتعاقبة في الزمان الماضي حيث اعترف المستدل بجريانه فيها وبين وجودها في الاستقبال إذ الموجود في كل زمان واحد من آحاد السلسلة ولو كفى الوجود الفرضي في الأمور الماضية كفى الوجود الفرضي في الأمور المستقبلة وحاصل الجواب إبداء الفرق بينهما بأن ما ضبطه الوجود فآحاد السلسلة الغير المتناهية فيها تكون موجودة في نفس الأمر ولو على التعاقب فيمكن فرض التطبيق بينها فرضاً مطابقاً للواقع فيلزم أحد المحالين بخلاف الأمور الموجودة في الاستقبال فإنها لم يضبطها الوجود فليست الآحاد موجودة في نفس الأمر ففرض التطبيق بينها فرض محال وعلى تقدير وقوعه إنما يستلزم تساوي ما فرض غير متساو أو تناهي ما فرض غير متناه ولا محذور في ذلك المحال يجوز أن يستلزم المحال كان الحادث في كل واحد من تلك الأجزاء واحداً أو أكثر فإن تناهيها مستلزم لتناهي آحادها لأن الحادث في كل زمان متناه. قوله: (والجواب عن هذا (النقض قال الأستاذ المحقق في الذخيرة واعلم أن معنى النقض جريان الدليل بجميع مقدماته في شيء مع تخلف الحكم عنه فجوابه إما بمنع جريان الدليل في صورة النقض لعدم صدق بعض مقدماته فيها وإما بمنع تخلف الحكم عنه فيها، فالمحققون
(And this proof has been objected to) by the ranks of numbers, because the proof applies to them despite their non-finiteness. That is because we assume two series of numbers: one is the multiplication of one an infinite number of times, and the other is the multiplication of a thousand similarly, then we align one with the other by placing the first of the excessive opposite the first of the deficient, and so on, while these two series are necessarily infinite. (And the answer) to this objection (is that the effects) — rather, concerning his saying ('for we assume, etc.') corresponding to what was said previously: as in Sharh al-Maqasid, that one assumes two series, one from one and the second from what is above it by a finite, and we align one with the other, etc. And the commentator (may his secret be sanctified) undertook the burden of multiplying one and multiplying what is above it an infinite number of times to obtain the two divergent series, and the application of alignment in them is more apparent than what was previously assumed from aligning individuals of a part with individuals of the whole. For if you say: previously it was alignment of one with one, and in the form of the objection on both appreciations it is alignment of one with many, I say: this difference is of no use because in each of them there is alignment of the finite with the finite, for if it entails a violation of assumption in the first, it entails a violation of assumption in the second, otherwise not. Then know that the running of the proof in numbers is not by virtue of their actual infinity — for no mutakallim holds that — because counted things are finite externally and mentally, and detailed conceptualization of them is impossible for limited powers, and the summary conceptualization has no multiplicity, let alone infinity. And in knowledge of Him (Exalted) they are finite necessarily due to the encompassing of knowledge, and likewise in the knowledge of the high principles if we affirm their existence, and detailed knowledge of them is of what is not infinite. Rather, its running in them is by virtue of their infinity in potentiality, by virtue of their existence in external counted things that are infinite in the future. And its source is the lack of distinction between the existence of successive things in past time — where the arguer acknowledged its running — and their existence in the future, since what exists in each time is one of the individuals of the series. And if hypothetical existence sufficed in past things, hypothetical existence would suffice in future things. The gist of the answer is showing the difference between them: that which existence has determined, the individuals of the infinite series in it exist in actuality, even if successively, so it is possible to assume alignment between them in an assumption that matches reality, so one of the two impossible things necessarily follows. In contrast, things existing in the future are not determined by existence, so the individuals do not exist in actuality, so assuming alignment between them is an impossible assumption, and if it were to occur, it would only entail equality of what was assumed unequal or finiteness of what was assumed infinite, and there is no harm in that impossibility being allowed to entail impossibility. What occurs in each part is one or more, for their finiteness entails the finiteness of their individuals because what occurs in each time is finite. His saying: (And the answer to this objection). The master investigator said in al-Dhakhira: Know that the meaning of objection (naqd) is the running of a proof with all its premises in something while the judgment is absent from it. So its answer is either by denying the running of the proof in the form of the objection due to the falsity of some of its premises in it, or by denying the absence of the judgment from it therein. So the investigators...
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage presents an objection to the proof of alignment (burhan al-tatbiq) based on infinite numbers, and provides a detailed answer. The objector argues that the proof would apply to series of numbers like doubling 1 and doubling 1000 infinitely — by aligning them, one should get a contradiction, yet both series are accepted as infinite (in the sense of potential infinity). The answer, drawing on Sharh al-Maqasid, clarifies that the proof does not apply to numbers in actuality because no mutakallim holds that numbers exist as an actual infinite; rather, numbers are potentially infinite in future external counted things. The crux of the answer is the distinction between what is 'determined by existence' (ma dabatuhu al-wujud) — past events that have actually occurred — and what is not yet determined (future events). In an actual infinite regress of past causes (like motions or effects), each individual has existed in reality, so aligning them yields a real contradiction. But for future numbers or events, they do not yet exist in actuality, so assuming alignment is an impossible assumption; if it were made, it would only produce a hypothetical contradiction that does not prove impossibility in reality. The passage also defines the technical meaning of 'objection' (naqd) as a proof applying yet the judgment not following, and indicates that the proper response is to deny either the applicability of the proof or the absence of the judgment. The text ends mid-sentence quoting al-Dhakhira.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The burhan al-tatbiq applies to any infinite series, including numbers.
Correction: The burhan al-tatbiq only applies to series where the individuals have actual existence (past events), not to potential infinities like numbers.

Checkpoint
How does the answer to the numbers objection distinguish between past and future series?
A) Past series are infinite in actuality, future series are finite.
B) Past series are determined by existence, so alignment is realistic; future series are not determined, so alignment is hypothetical and harmless.
C) Past series are linear, future series are circular.
D) The proof only works for causes, not for numbers.

Key Takeaway
The burhan al-tatbiq only yields contradictions for actual infinite regresses where individuals have existed, not for potential infinities like numbers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you plan for your future, do you treat your intentions as actual realities or as mere possibilities? How does the distinction between actual and potential infinity challenge you to entrust your future to Allah rather than assume control over what does not yet exist?
?
Are there past sins you keep reliving as if they were still present, creating an 'actual infinite' of guilt? How can the lesson's emphasis on only actual existences being subject to real consequences help you break free from such a cycle?
?
If Allah's knowledge encompasses all future events as actual in His knowledge but potential in their occurrence, how does this affect your understanding of divine decree and your responsibility to act? Will you let this truth increase your reliance on Him or your negligence?

Conditions of the Burhan al-Tatbiq: Coexistence and Order
Explanation of the necessity of coexistence and order for the Burhan al-Tatbiq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two necessary conditions for the Burhan al-Tatbiq and the refutation of the objection that gradual existence suffices.

Core Idea
The Burhan al-Tatbiq requires coexistence and order to refute regress.

In this passage, Sanusi examines the logical conditions required for the Burhan al-Tatbiq, the argument of parallel alignment used to disprove infinite regress. He explains that the two series must exist together in detail and be ordered relative to each other. The passage then addresses a potential objection and teases out the precise meaning of alignment.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then the English translation. Let the author's own argument come through.
The passage is dense; read slowly.
2
Identify the two conditions for alignment
Find where Sanusi states that alignment requires the series to exist together (coexistence) and to have order (tartīb).
These are the core conditions for the Burhan al-Tatbiq to work.
3
Understand the refutation of gradual existence
The objector says alignment can happen gradually. Sanusi argues that each stage still requires simultaneous existence of both sides.
This shows why coexistence is essential at every step.
4
Analyze the discussion on 'one opposite one'
Sanusi distinguishes two interpretations of the opponent's claim: one about corresponding positions, one about one-to-one correspondence. He accepts the first but rejects the second.
This clarifies what alignment actually requires.
5
Reflect on the significance
Consider how this argument prevents infinite regress. The conditions ensure that the two series are comparable and cannot be infinite.
This ties back to the broader goal of proving the ending of chains.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الخامس - المقصد الثامن : التسلسل محال أن يستند الممكن إلى علة مفصلة في الذهن دفعة ومن المعلوم أنه لا يتصور وقوع بعضها بازاء بعض إلا إذا كانت موجودة تفصيلاً معاً إما في الخارج أو في الذهن وكذا لا يتم التطبيق إذا كانت الآحاد موجودة معاً ، ولم يكن بينها ترتب بوجه ما إذ لا يلزم من كون الأول بإزاء الأول واعتبر وقوع بعض الآحاد بإزاء بعض حكم بأنها تستلزم أحد المحلين المذكورين، وأما ما قيل في بيان عدم اشتراط الاجتماع من أن وجود كل واحد في وقت يكفي للانطباق ووقوع كل واحد الآحاد بإزاء الآخر غاية الأمر أن يكون التطبيق تدريجياً فمدفوع بأنه وإن كان تدريجياً لا بد كل مرتبة من وجود الطرفين معاً ولا وجود في السلسلة المتعاقبة إلا للواحد فقط . قوله : ( إذ لا يلزم إلخ) فيه أنه إن أراد به لا يلزم وقوع واحد بإزاء ما كان نظيره في الترتيب من الجملة الأخرى فمسلم لكنا لا نعتبر في التطبيق ذلك ولا نحتاج إليه إذ ليس مقصودنا إثبات الانتهاء إلى ما هو طرف السلسلة بل الانتهاء مطلقاً وإن أراد به أنه لا يلزم وقوع واحد بإزاء واحد كما يدل عليه لجواز أن يقع آحاد كثيرة من إحداهما بإزاء واحد من الأخرى فممنوع لأنه بعد ما كان الآحاد موجودة إمكان وقوع واحد بإزاء واحد لازم وذلك كاف في المقصود وجواز وقوع آحاد كثيرة بإزاء واحد لا يقدح في ذلك كما لا يخفى وبما ذكرنا لك ظهر علو ما قاله الإمام في المطالب العالية أنه استقر رأيي بعد الأفكار المتتالية مدة أربعين يوماً متوالية على أن هذا الضبط التطبيق ولا يتوقف على الاجتماع والترتب فتدبر فإنه مما خفي على بعض الناظرين وتصدى لبيان الاشتراط المذكور بمقدمات يظهر فسادها مما حررناه .
The Fifth Observatory - The Eighth Intention: That regress is impossible: it is impossible for the contingent to be based on a cause detailed in the mind at once. And it is known that it is not conceivable for some of them to occur opposite some others unless they exist in detail together, either in the external world or in the mind. Similarly, the alignment is not possible if the individuals exist together but there is no order between them in any way, because it does not necessarily follow from the first being opposite the first, and he considered the occurrence of some individuals opposite some and judged that they entail one of the two mentioned loci. As for what was said in explaining the non-requirement of co-existence, that the existence of each one at a time suffices for the alignment and the occurrence of each individual opposite the other, the only thing being that the alignment is gradual, it is refuted by the fact that even if it is gradual, each stage requires the existence of both sides together, and in the successive series only one exists. His saying: (Since it does not follow, etc.) There is in it: If he means by it that it does not require the occurrence of one opposite its counterpart in order from the other series, then it is granted, but we do not consider that in the alignment nor do we need it, because our purpose is not to prove the ending at the extremity of the series, but rather the ending absolutely. And if he means by it that it does not require the occurrence of one opposite one, as indicated by the possibility that many individuals from one of them occur opposite one from the other, then it is denied, because once the individuals exist, the possibility of one occurring opposite one is necessary, and that is sufficient for the purpose, and the possibility of many individuals occurring opposite one does not harm that, as is not hidden. And by what we have mentioned to you, the highness of what the Imam said in al-Matalib al-Aliya becomes apparent: that his opinion settled after successive thoughts for forty consecutive days that this regulation is the alignment and it does not depend on co-existence and order. So ponder, for it is among what was hidden from some investigators and he undertook to explain the mentioned condition with premises whose corruption appears from what we have set forth.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage defines the condition for the Burhan al-Tatbiq (the argument of parallel alignment). It begins by stating that for the argument to work, the two series (e.g., causes and effects) must exist together in detail in the mind or externally, and there must be an order between them. If they are merely successive without coexistence, alignment fails because at any given moment only one member exists. The author then refutes an objection that gradual existence suffices, arguing that each stage still requires both sides to exist simultaneously. Then he comments on a previous statement (قوله) distinguishing two interpretations: if the opponent means we need not align corresponding positions in order, that is granted but unnecessary; if they mean we need not align one-to-one, that is denied because once individuals exist, the possibility of one-to-one alignment is necessary. He concludes by citing al-Razi's view that after forty days of thought, he concluded that the alignment does not require coexistence and order, but the author implies that this view is problematic.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Gradual existence of the two series is sufficient for the Burhan al-Tatbiq to work.
Correction: Even if alignment is gradual, each stage requires simultaneous existence of both sides; in a successive series only one exists at a time, so coexistence is necessary.

Checkpoint
What condition does the Burhan al-Tatbiq require for the two series?
A) Coexistence and order
B) Only coexistence
C) Only order
D) Neither coexistence nor order

Key Takeaway
The Burhan al-Tatbiq to disprove regress requires that the two series coexist in detail and be ordered; otherwise the alignment fails.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author mentions that Imam al-Razi spent forty consecutive days in thought before settling his view. What belief do you hold, even subconsciously, that you have never subjected to such rigorous scrutiny? Will you commit to examining it with the same intensity this week?
?
If alignment requires coexistence and order, your spiritual states (ikhlas, khushu') cannot be built piecemeal—they must be present together. In which part of your worship have you been satisfied with gradual improvement without seeking immediate presence? What step will you take today to bring your heart into full alignment with Allah?
?
The argument shows that without order, alignment fails. Your life is a series of choices—are they ordered toward your ultimate end (hereafter)? Or is there disorder (shirk of intentions, worldly priorities) that prevents the proof of your faith from being valid? What must you reorder starting now?

First Objection: Intellect Cannot Handle Infinite Detail
First sub-objection against necessity of order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first objection against the necessity of order in Burhan al-Tatbiq, which argues that one-to-one mapping is not required because alignment can occur without order and the intellect cannot process infinite detail.

Core Idea
Alignment without order is possible if the intellect cannot handle infinite detail.

The first objection challenges the assumption that ordered alignment is necessary for the Burhan al-Tatbiq. It argues that a one-to-one correspondence can occur without any inherent order, and that the intellect's inability to process infinite details undermines the standard proof. This lesson examines the objection and its supporting example of two mountains and pebbles.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Try to grasp the overall argument.
2
Identify the main claim
The objection claims that alignment can happen without order—e.g., first-to-first, second-to-second—because many individuals from one series can correspond to one from the other.
This is a key point: order is not strictly required.
3
Analyze the mountain-pebble analogy
The example of two mountains and pebbles shows that aligning edges suffices for a one-to-one correspondence, but for pebbles you need detailed pairing. Understand the contrast.
This illustrates the difference between continuous and discrete alignment.
4
Understand the conclusion
The objectors conclude that both coexistence and order are needed for the proof to work, so the Burhan al-Tatbiq cannot be refuted by unordered infinite series.
This sets up the next two objections.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وكذا لا يتم التطبيق إذا كانت الآحاد موجودة معاً ولم يكن بينها ترتب بوجه ما فيه بحث أما أولاً : فلان وقوع كل واحد من آحاد الجملة الناقصة بإزاء واحد من آحاد الجملة التامة بأن يعلم ذاتها مع مالها من ل ليس بالضروري كما زعم بل يمكن أن يكون من غير ترتب بأن يقع الأول بإزاء الأول والثاني بإزاء الثاني والثالث بإزاء الثالث وهكذا لجواز أن يقع آحاد كثيرة من إحداهما بإزاء واحد من الأخرى اللهم إلا إذا لاحظ العقل كل واحد من الأولى واعتبره بإزاء واحد من الأخرى لكن العقل لا يقدر على استحضار ما لا نهاية له مفصلة لا دفعة ولا في زمان متناه حتى يتصور هناك تطبيق ويظهر الخلف بل ينقطع التطبيق بانقطاع الوهم والعقل واستوضح ما صورناه لك بتوهم التطبيق بين جبلين ممتدين على الاستواء أعداد الحصى فإنك في الأول إذا طبقت طرف أحد الجبلين على طرف الآخر وبين كان ذلك كافياً في وقوع كل جزء من أحدهما بإزاء جزء من الثاني وليس الحال في أعداد الحصى كذلك بل لا بد لك في التطبيق من اعتبار تفاصيلها قالوا : فقد ظهر أنه لا بد من هذين القيدين في تتميم البرهان التطبيقي فلا نقض بالأعداد أصلا وأما ثانيا فلان عقولنا وإن كانت لا تقدر على استحضار ما لا نهاية له مفصلة إلا أن القوى العالية وافية بملاحظتها وتطبيقها فيرد الإشكال وأما ثالثاً فلان الجملتين إن لزم كونهما متحققتين في نفس الأمر بحيث يحصل التطبيق بينهما فيها، لم يتم الدليل لأنه لا يلزم استحالة وجود سلسلة واحدة غير متناهية . إذ ليس هناك جملتان متحققتان في نفس الأمر متطابقتان لتوقف ذلك على تباين الجملتين وانفصالهما والجزء مع الكل ليس كذلك وحديث الجبلين والرمل الذي أورده للتوضيح ضائع إذ لا مناسبة له بما نحن بصدده. وإن كفى كون الجملتين والتطبيق بينهما فرضيات محضة فالدليل جار في غير المرتب بل في مراتب الأعداد أيضاً وهذا الثالث وارد على المتكلمين أيضاً في مراتب الأعداد.
His saying: (And likewise the alignment is not possible if the individuals exist together but there is no order between them in any way). There is discussion in it. First: The occurrence of each individual of the incomplete series opposite one individual of the complete series by knowing its essence with what it has of [؟] is not necessary as claimed; rather it can be without order, such that the first occurs opposite the first, the second opposite the second, the third opposite the third, and so on, because it is possible that many individuals from one of them occur opposite one from the other, unless the intellect observes each one of the first and considers it opposite one from the other. But the intellect cannot summon the infinite in detail, neither at once nor in finite time, so that there could be an alignment and the contradiction would appear; rather the alignment is cut off by the cessation of estimation and intellect. And he clarified what we have pictured for you by imagining the alignment between two mountains extending evenly with the number of pebbles: for in the first, if you align the edge of one mountain with the edge of the other and between, that is sufficient for the occurrence of each part of one opposite a part of the other. But the case is not so with the number of pebbles; rather you must in the alignment consider their particulars. They said: So it has become apparent that these two restrictions are necessary for completing the Burhan al-Tatbiq, so no refutation by numbers at all. Second: Our intellects, even if they cannot summon the infinite in detail, yet the higher powers are sufficient to observe them and align them, so the problem arises. Third: If it is necessary that the two series be actualized in reality such that the alignment occurs between them, then the proof is not established because it does not necessitate the impossibility of a single infinite series; for there are not two series actualized in reality that correspond, because that depends on the distinction and separation of the two series, and the part with the whole is not like that. And the talk of the two mountains and sand which he brought for clarification is wasted, for there is no relevance to what we are about. And if it suffices that the two series and the alignment between them are purely hypothetical, then the proof applies to the non-ordered, indeed to the ranks of numbers as well. And this third [point] applies to the theologians also in the ranks of numbers.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage presents three objections (أما أولاً, ثانياً, ثالثاً) against the requirement of order for the Burhan al-Tatbiq. The first objection argues that one-to-one alignment is not necessary because it is possible that many individuals from one series align with a single individual from the other; the intellect cannot handle infinite detail anyway, so the argument using the example of two mountains and pebbles shows that alignment can be done without order. The objectors conclude that both coexistence and order are needed. The second objection states that even if human intellect cannot handle infinite detail, higher powers (e.g., celestial intellects) can, so the problem remains. The third objection argues that if the two series must be actual in reality, then the proof fails because a single infinite chain is impossible only if there are two distinct series; but a part and its whole are not two distinct series. The objector claims that if the series are merely hypothetical, the proof applies even to unordered things like numbers. The author then notes that this third point also refutes the theologians' argument regarding numbers.

Key Terms
برهان التطبيق
الترتب
الجملة الناقصة
الجملة التامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that ordered alignment is absolutely necessary for Burhan al-Tatbiq to work.
Correction: This objection shows that alignment can occur without order if the intellect cannot process infinite details, so order is not strictly necessary.

Checkpoint
What does the mountain-pebble analogy illustrate in the first objection?
A) That both mountains and pebbles require detailed ordering
B) That alignment of mountain edges suffices for part-to-part correspondence without ordering
C) That pebbles can be aligned without order
D) That the intellect can handle infinite details

Key Takeaway
The first objection claims that alignment without order is possible, and the intellect's inability to grasp infinite detail prevents the standard proof from working.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The objector claims that the intellect cannot summon infinite detail. When you think about Allah's attributes like His knowledge encompassing all things, do you ever feel overwhelmed by your own inability to fully comprehend? How does this limitation affect your trust in rational proofs versus reliance on revelation?
?
In the mountain-and-pebbles analogy, continuous alignment suffices for continuous surfaces but not for discrete items. Which better describes your spiritual life: a continuous flow of obedience or a collection of individual acts? What would it take to bring more coherence and order to your deeds?
?
If the intellect cannot grasp infinite detail, then your understanding of any proof must be humble. Are you willing to accept that some truths may be beyond your full comprehension, even while you hold them firmly? What would change if you truly internalized that your mind has limits?

Second Objection: Higher Powers Can Observe Infinite Detail
Second sub-objection: higher powers bypass human limitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second objection, which argues that even if human intellect is limited, higher powers (e.g., celestial intellects) can observe infinite detail, thus reviving the original problem.

Core Idea
Higher powers can handle infinite detail, so the problem remains.

The first objection relied on the limitation of human intellect. The second objection counters that even if humans cannot grasp infinite details, higher powers such as celestial intellects can. This lesson explains how this objection reopens the problem for the Burhan al-Tatbiq.

Guided Path
1
Read the short passage
Read the Arabic and translation for the second objection. Note it is very brief.
2
Understand the premise
The objection acknowledges that human intellect is limited regarding infinite detail, but higher powers (al-quwwa al-‘aliya) are not.
Higher powers refer to celestial intellects or divine knowledge.
3
See the consequence
Since higher powers can observe and align infinite details, the problem of infinite series arises again.
This undermines the first objection's reliance on human limitation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وكذا لا يتم التطبيق إذا كانت الآحاد موجودة معاً ولم يكن بينها ترتب بوجه ما فيه بحث أما أولاً : فلان وقوع كل واحد من آحاد الجملة الناقصة بإزاء واحد من آحاد الجملة التامة بأن يعلم ذاتها مع مالها من ل ليس بالضروري كما زعم بل يمكن أن يكون من غير ترتب بأن يقع الأول بإزاء الأول والثاني بإزاء الثاني والثالث بإزاء الثالث وهكذا لجواز أن يقع آحاد كثيرة من إحداهما بإزاء واحد من الأخرى اللهم إلا إذا لاحظ العقل كل واحد من الأولى واعتبره بإزاء واحد من الأخرى لكن العقل لا يقدر على استحضار ما لا نهاية له مفصلة لا دفعة ولا في زمان متناه حتى يتصور هناك تطبيق ويظهر الخلف بل ينقطع التطبيق بانقطاع الوهم والعقل واستوضح ما صورناه لك بتوهم التطبيق بين جبلين ممتدين على الاستواء أعداد الحصى فإنك في الأول إذا طبقت طرف أحد الجبلين على طرف الآخر وبين كان ذلك كافياً في وقوع كل جزء من أحدهما بإزاء جزء من الثاني وليس الحال في أعداد الحصى كذلك بل لا بد لك في التطبيق من اعتبار تفاصيلها قالوا : فقد ظهر أنه لا بد من هذين القيدين في تتميم البرهان التطبيقي فلا نقض بالأعداد أصلا وأما ثانيا فلان عقولنا وإن كانت لا تقدر على استحضار ما لا نهاية له مفصلة إلا أن القوى العالية وافية بملاحظتها وتطبيقها فيرد الإشكال وأما ثالثاً فلان الجملتين إن لزم كونهما متحققتين في نفس الأمر بحيث يحصل التطبيق بينهما فيها، لم يتم الدليل لأنه لا يلزم استحالة وجود سلسلة واحدة غير متناهية . إذ ليس هناك جملتان متحققتان في نفس الأمر متطابقتان لتوقف ذلك على تباين الجملتين وانفصالهما والجزء مع الكل ليس كذلك وحديث الجبلين والرمل الذي أورده للتوضيح ضائع إذ لا مناسبة له بما نحن بصدده. وإن كفى كون الجملتين والتطبيق بينهما فرضيات محضة فالدليل جار في غير المرتب بل في مراتب الأعداد أيضاً وهذا الثالث وارد على المتكلمين أيضاً في مراتب الأعداد.
His saying: (And likewise the alignment is not possible if the individuals exist together but there is no order between them in any way). There is discussion in it. First: The occurrence of each individual of the incomplete series opposite one individual of the complete series by knowing its essence with what it has of [؟] is not necessary as claimed; rather it can be without order, such that the first occurs opposite the first, the second opposite the second, the third opposite the third, and so on, because it is possible that many individuals from one of them occur opposite one from the other, unless the intellect observes each one of the first and considers it opposite one from the other. But the intellect cannot summon the infinite in detail, neither at once nor in finite time, so that there could be an alignment and the contradiction would appear; rather the alignment is cut off by the cessation of estimation and intellect. And he clarified what we have pictured for you by imagining the alignment between two mountains extending evenly with the number of pebbles: for in the first, if you align the edge of one mountain with the edge of the other and between, that is sufficient for the occurrence of each part of one opposite a part of the other. But the case is not so with the number of pebbles; rather you must in the alignment consider their particulars. They said: So it has become apparent that these two restrictions are necessary for completing the Burhan al-Tatbiq, so no refutation by numbers at all. Second: Our intellects, even if they cannot summon the infinite in detail, yet the higher powers are sufficient to observe them and align them, so the problem arises. Third: If it is necessary that the two series be actualized in reality such that the alignment occurs between them, then the proof is not established because it does not necessitate the impossibility of a single infinite series; for there are not two series actualized in reality that correspond, because that depends on the distinction and separation of the two series, and the part with the whole is not like that. And the talk of the two mountains and sand which he brought for clarification is wasted, for there is no relevance to what we are about. And if it suffices that the two series and the alignment between them are purely hypothetical, then the proof applies to the non-ordered, indeed to the ranks of numbers as well. And this third [point] applies to the theologians also in the ranks of numbers.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage presents three objections (أما أولاً, ثانياً, ثالثاً) against the requirement of order for the Burhan al-Tatbiq. The first objection argues that one-to-one alignment is not necessary because it is possible that many individuals from one series align with a single individual from the other; the intellect cannot handle infinite detail anyway, so the argument using the example of two mountains and pebbles shows that alignment can be done without order. The objectors conclude that both coexistence and order are needed. The second objection states that even if human intellect cannot handle infinite detail, higher powers (e.g., celestial intellects) can, so the problem remains. The third objection argues that if the two series must be actual in reality, then the proof fails because a single infinite chain is impossible only if there are two distinct series; but a part and its whole are not two distinct series. The objector claims that if the series are merely hypothetical, the proof applies even to unordered things like numbers. The author then notes that this third point also refutes the theologians' argument regarding numbers.

Key Terms
القوى العالية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the first objection's reliance on human intellectual limitation is sufficient to refute the Burhan al-Tatbiq.
Correction: The second objection shows that higher powers can handle infinite detail, so the problem remains.

Checkpoint
What is the key claim of the second objection?
A) Human intellect can grasp infinite details if given enough time
B) Higher powers can observe and align infinite details
C) The Burhan al-Tatbiq is valid only for finite series
D) Order is necessary for alignment

Key Takeaway
Even if humans cannot grasp infinite detail, higher powers can, so the original problem of infinite series persists.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If higher powers—ultimately God—observe every infinite detail of your existence, what sins do you still commit as if no one is watching? What would it mean to live today with the certainty that nothing is hidden?
?
Your intellect cannot grasp the full detail of your own life, yet God's knowledge encompasses it completely. How does this truth compel you to trust His judgment over your own, especially in areas where you question His wisdom?

Third Objection: Actual vs Hypothetical Series
Third sub-objection: actual vs hypothetical series

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third objection, which distinguishes between actual and hypothetical series and argues that if the series are merely hypothetical, the proof applies even to unordered things like numbers.

Core Idea
If series are hypothetical, the proof works even without order; if actual, a single infinite chain is possible.

The third objection is the most sweeping. It splits into two cases: if the two series are actual in reality, then no impossibility follows because a single infinite chain is possible (since part and whole are not two distinct series). If they are merely hypothetical, the proof applies even to unordered numbers. This lesson examines the ramifications for the Burhan al-Tatbiq and for theologians.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the third objection carefully. It has two conditional parts.
2
Understand the first case (actual series)
If the two series are actual in reality, the proof fails because a single infinite chain is possible—part and whole are not two series.
This challenges the requirement of two distinct series.
3
Understand the second case (hypothetical series)
If the series are merely hypothetical, the Burhan al-Tatbiq applies even to unordered things like numbers, so it fails to prove impossibility.
4
Note the implication
The objection concludes that this third point also applies to the theologians' argument about numbers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The Generality of Burhan al-Tatbiq and the Danger of Restricting It
Author asserts the Burhan al-Tatbiq is general and restricting it invalidates the proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Burhan al-Tatbiq must be applied universally and why restricting it undermines its validity.

Core Idea
Restricting the Burhan al-Tatbiq admits a counterexample and destroys the proof.

The author now delivers his decisive response to the objection. He asserts that the Burhan al-Tatbiq is inherently general, applying to all things encompassed by existence. To limit its conclusion to only ordered and coexistent things is to concede that the proof fails elsewhere — which means it is invalid.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the author's direct tone and logical structure.
The passage is dense but clear.
2
Identify the author's claim
The author states that the Burhan al-Tatbiq is 'general' (عام) and applies to everything existence encompasses. Highlight this key point.
Generality is the foundation of the argument.
3
Understand the consequence of restriction
If someone restricts the conclusion to only cases with coexistence and order, they admit that the proof fails for other cases. This 'counterexample' (نقض) invalidates the proof.
The proof must be universal to be sound.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال المصنف : وأنت تعلم أن الدليل يعنى برهان التطبيق عام لقيامه وجريانه في كل ما ضبطه وجود كما قررناه لك فتخصيص المدلول ببعض ذلك المضبوط أعني المقيد بالاجتماع في الوجود مع الترتب بوجه من الوجوه اعتراف بالتخلف أي بتخلف المدلول عن الدليل في البعض الآخر أعني الحوادث المتعاقبة والأمور المجتمعة بلا ترتب وأنه يوجب بطلان الدليل لكونه منقوضاً .
The author said: And you know that the proof, meaning the Burhan al-Tatbiq, is general in its validity and running in everything that existence encompasses, as we have established for you. So restricting the conclusion to some of that encompassed, namely that which is restricted by coexistence in existence with order in some way, is an admission of a counterexample, i.e., that the conclusion fails for the other part, namely successive events and things that coexist without order, and that necessitates the invalidity of the proof because it is refuted.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage is the author's direct response to the objection that the Burhan al-Tatbiq requires coexistence and order. He states that the proof is general and applies to all things that have existence (كل ما ضبطه وجود). Therefore, if one restricts the conclusion only to cases with coexistence and order, that is an admission that the proof does not apply to other cases (successive events or unordered coexistent things). Such an admission means the proof is invalid because it is refuted (منقوض) by a counterexample.

Key Terms
برهان التطبيق
عام
المدلول
التخلف
النقض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the Burhan al-Tatbiq can be legitimately restricted to ordered coexistent series without affecting its validity.
Correction: The author argues that any restriction admits a counterexample for other cases (e.g., successive events or unordered coexistence), which invalidates the proof.

Checkpoint
What does restricting the conclusion of the Burhan al-Tatbiq to ordered series imply?
A) The proof becomes stronger
B) It admits a counterexample and invalidates the proof
C) It shows the proof is specific
D) It preserves the proof's generality

Key Takeaway
The Burhan al-Tatbiq is universally general; any restriction admits a counterexample and renders the proof invalid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever justified restricting a clear Islamic principle to avoid applying it to a difficult situation in your life? What would the author of this passage say to you about that restriction?
?
If the Burhan al-Tatbiq must be general to be valid, where in your faith do you try to limit general commands to avoid personal cost? What counterexample in your own actions invalidates your claim to follow the truth?
?
This passage warns that admitting exceptions destroys a proof. In your relationship with Allah, are there areas where you treat His commands as general for others but make exceptions for yourself? How would you feel if Allah restricted His mercy to only some of your sins?

The Condition Can Be Non-Existent
Argues condition can be non-existent, defines condition as dependence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that a condition (shart) can be non-existent, contrary to the view of some scholars, and that it is defined by dependence, not causation.

Core Idea
A condition is about dependence, not existence.

This passage addresses a foundational question in causal chains: must a condition be something that exists? The author argues that non-existence can serve as a condition, just as the absence of opposites is a condition for knowledge. Let’s examine the reasoning and the opposing view.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on non-existential condition
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice the definition of condition given and how the author argues that non-existence is not impossible.
The key phrase: 'لا معنى للشرط إلا ما يتوقف المشروط في وجوده عليه'.
2
Identify the two positions
The passage presents the author's view that condition can be non-existent, and then mentions that some scholars insist conditions must be existent. Compare the two.
The author does not specify who holds the opposing view.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this distinction matters: if conditions could only be existent, many logical dependencies would be excluded. Think of an example like the absence of fire being a condition for safety.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يمتنع لا يمتنع أن يكون الشرط عدمياً كانتفاء أضداد العلم بالنسبة إلى وجوده، إذ لا معنى للشرط إلا ما يتوقف المشروط في وجوده عليه لا ما يؤثر في وجود المشروط، حتى أن يكون عدمياً. وذهب بعضهم إلى أن الشرط لا بد أن يكون وجودياً. ( الثالث : أنه قد يكون ) الشرط ( متعدداً)، بأن يكون لمشروط واحد شروط يلزم انتفاؤه بانتفاء كل واحد منها كالحياة وانتفاء الأضداد بالنسبة إلى وجود العلم، أو مركباً بأن يكون عدة أمور شرطاً واحداً للمشروط . الرابع: الشرط قد يكون محل الحكم، والعلة صفته يعني أن محل الحكم لا يجوز أن يكون علة للحكم؛ لأنه لا يكون مؤثراً، بل المؤثر فيه صفة ذلك المحل التي هي العلة، كما عرفت لكن محل الحكم يكون شرطاً للحكم من حيث يتوقف وجوده عليه. قوله : (الشرط) أي بلا واسطة، فظهر انقسامه إلى المتعدد والمركب، وعدم ورود أن أجزاء المركب أيضاً شروط فيكون متعدداً. قوله : (كما عرفت من أن العلة صفة توجب لمحلها حكماً . قوله: (يكون شرطاً للحكم إلخ) أي من حيث يتوقف وجود العلة علية، وذلك إذا كانت العلة قائمة بمحل الحكم، وكل ما هو شرط لوجود العلة شرط للحكم، وقد لا يكون شرطاً للحكم؛ بناء على جواز كون العلة خارجة عن محل الحكم وإنما قيد بالحيثية؛ لامتناع توقف الحكم عليه لا من هذه الحيثية، لامتناع توقف إيجاب العلة على شرط . قوله : ( أو مركباً) الفرق بينه وبين المتعدد مع أن الموقوف على المركب موقوف على كل من أجزائه، فيتعدد الموقوف عليه هاهنا أيضاً، أن التوقف هاهنا بالذات على المجموع، والتوقف على الأجزاء بالواسطة، ولا كذلك الحال في المتعدد وأيضاً المركب ماهية واحدة، ولا كذلك المتعدد المذكور. قوله : (لأنه لا يكون مؤثراً لا لان الشيء الواحد لا يكون قابلاً وفاعلاً، بل لضرورة أن العالمية لا تعلل بغير العلم، وهو ليس محلاً لها .
It is not impossible for the condition to be non-existent, like the absence of opposites of knowledge relative to its existence, for there is no meaning of condition except that upon which the conditioned depends in its existence, not that which affects the existence of the conditioned, so that it may be non-existent. Some held that the condition must be existential. Third: The condition may be multiple, meaning that for one conditioned there are conditions such that its non-existence follows from the non-existence of each one, like life and the absence of opposites relative to the existence of knowledge; or composite, meaning that several things are one condition for the conditioned. Fourth: The condition may be the locus of the judgment, and the cause is its attribute, meaning that the locus of the judgment may not be a cause for the judgment because it does not affect, rather what affects is the attribute of that locus which is the cause, as you have learned; but the locus of the judgment is a condition for the judgment insofar as its existence depends on it. [Commentary:] His saying: (the condition) i.e. without mediation, so its division into multiple and composite becomes apparent, and it is not valid that the parts of the composite are also conditions, making it multiple. His saying: (as you have learned that the cause is an attribute that necessitates a judgment for its locus). His saying: (it is a condition for the judgment etc.) i.e. insofar as the existence of the cause depends on it, and that is when the cause is inherent in the locus of the judgment, and whatever is a condition for the existence of the cause is a condition for the judgment, and it may not be a condition for the judgment based on the permissibility of the cause being external to the locus of the judgment; he restricted it with 'insofar as' because it is impossible for the judgment to depend on it apart from this respect, due to the impossibility of the effect depending on a condition. His saying: (or composite) the difference between it and the multiple—even though what depends on the composite depends on each of its parts, so that upon which it depends also becomes multiple here—is that the dependence here is essentially on the whole, and dependence on the parts is by mediation, and this is not the case in the multiple; also, the composite is a single essence, and this is not the case with the multiple mentioned. His saying: (because it does not affect) not because a single thing cannot be both receptive and active, but because it is necessary that the attribute of being knowing is not caused by other than knowledge, and it is not a locus for it.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage defines the nature of a condition (shart) in the context of causal relationships. It begins by stating that a condition may be non-existent, such as the absence of opposites of knowledge being a condition for the existence of knowledge. The author clarifies that a condition is merely that upon which the conditioned depends, not that which produces an effect. Some scholars, however, require the condition to be existent. The passage then lists two types of conditions under a third point: a condition may be multiple, meaning several independent conditions each necessary for the conditioned, like life and the absence of opposites for knowledge; or composite, meaning several things together form a single condition. The fourth point discusses the condition as the locus of the judgment: the locus itself is not a cause but its attribute is the cause; however, the locus is a condition for the judgment because the judgment's existence depends on the locus. The commentary then explains that the condition here is without mediation, and distinguishes between multiple and composite conditions: for a composite, dependence is directly on the whole, while for parts it is indirect, whereas for multiple conditions each is directly necessary. The commentary also explains that when the cause is inherent in the locus, the condition for the cause's existence is also a condition for the judgment, but if the cause is external, it may not hold. Finally, the commentary addresses why the locus cannot be a cause: a single thing cannot be both receptive and active, and the attribute of being knowing is not caused by anything other than knowledge itself.

Key Terms
شرط (shart)
عدم (non-existence)
مشروط (mashrut)
أضداد (opposites)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A condition must always be something that exists.
Correction: A condition is defined by dependence, not existence; non-existence (like absence of an obstacle) can be a condition.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why can a condition be non-existent?
A) Because non-existence is a kind of existence.
B) Because the condition is defined as that upon which the conditioned depends, not as a cause.
C) Because all scholars agree on this.
D) Because non-existence can affect the conditioned.

Key Takeaway
A condition can be non-existent because it is defined by dependence, not by being a cause.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your understanding of your own faith, do you tend to view Allah's conditions for guidance (like repentance) as causes that 'produce' forgiveness, or as dependencies that make you receptive? Which view makes you more reliant on Him?
?
Think of a struggle in your life, like the absence of a bad habit. Is that absence merely a 'non-existent condition' for growth, or do you treat it as a cause? How does this lesson challenge you to see God's role in your change?
?
If a condition can be non-existent, then even your 'lack' of something can be a valid prerequisite for divine mercy. How does that change the way you assess your own spiritual state—are you looking for existent qualifications or recognizing non-existent dependencies?

Logic and Technical Terms
intermediate
6 min
Multiple and Composite Conditions
Defines and distinguishes multiple and composite conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a multiple condition (several independent conditions for one thing) and a composite condition (several things together as one condition).

Core Idea
Multiple conditions are independent; a composite condition is a single unit.

When one thing depends on several conditions, those conditions can be either independent of each other or combined into one composite condition. This passage explains both types and clarifies the distinction through examples and logical analysis.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on multiple and composite conditions
Study the Arabic text and translation, focusing on the definitions and the example of life and absence of opposites for knowledge.
The example: for knowledge to exist, both life and absence of opposites are needed. Are they multiple or composite?
2
Compare the two types
Note the key difference: for multiple conditions, each is individually necessary; for composite, the whole is a single condition, and the parts are conditions only indirectly.
The commentary elaborates: dependence on a composite is directly on the whole, while dependence on multiple is directly on each.
3
Consider a counterargument
The commentary mentions an objection: parts of composite could be seen as multiple conditions. Understand why it's not valid: the composite is a single essence, unlike multiple conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يمتنع لا يمتنع أن يكون الشرط عدمياً كانتفاء أضداد العلم بالنسبة إلى وجوده، إذ لا معنى للشرط إلا ما يتوقف المشروط في وجوده عليه لا ما يؤثر في وجود المشروط، حتى أن يكون عدمياً. وذهب بعضهم إلى أن الشرط لا بد أن يكون وجودياً. ( الثالث : أنه قد يكون ) الشرط ( متعدداً)، بأن يكون لمشروط واحد شروط يلزم انتفاؤه بانتفاء كل واحد منها كالحياة وانتفاء الأضداد بالنسبة إلى وجود العلم، أو مركباً بأن يكون عدة أمور شرطاً واحداً للمشروط . الرابع: الشرط قد يكون محل الحكم، والعلة صفته يعني أن محل الحكم لا يجوز أن يكون علة للحكم؛ لأنه لا يكون مؤثراً، بل المؤثر فيه صفة ذلك المحل التي هي العلة، كما عرفت لكن محل الحكم يكون شرطاً للحكم من حيث يتوقف وجوده عليه. قوله : (الشرط) أي بلا واسطة، فظهر انقسامه إلى المتعدد والمركب، وعدم ورود أن أجزاء المركب أيضاً شروط فيكون متعدداً. قوله : (كما عرفت من أن العلة صفة توجب لمحلها حكماً . قوله: (يكون شرطاً للحكم إلخ) أي من حيث يتوقف وجود العلة علية، وذلك إذا كانت العلة قائمة بمحل الحكم، وكل ما هو شرط لوجود العلة شرط للحكم، وقد لا يكون شرطاً للحكم؛ بناء على جواز كون العلة خارجة عن محل الحكم وإنما قيد بالحيثية؛ لامتناع توقف الحكم عليه لا من هذه الحيثية، لامتناع توقف إيجاب العلة على شرط . قوله : ( أو مركباً) الفرق بينه وبين المتعدد مع أن الموقوف على المركب موقوف على كل من أجزائه، فيتعدد الموقوف عليه هاهنا أيضاً، أن التوقف هاهنا بالذات على المجموع، والتوقف على الأجزاء بالواسطة، ولا كذلك الحال في المتعدد وأيضاً المركب ماهية واحدة، ولا كذلك المتعدد المذكور. قوله : (لأنه لا يكون مؤثراً لا لان الشيء الواحد لا يكون قابلاً وفاعلاً، بل لضرورة أن العالمية لا تعلل بغير العلم، وهو ليس محلاً لها .
It is not impossible for the condition to be non-existent, like the absence of opposites of knowledge relative to its existence, for there is no meaning of condition except that upon which the conditioned depends in its existence, not that which affects the existence of the conditioned, so that it may be non-existent. Some held that the condition must be existential. Third: The condition may be multiple, meaning that for one conditioned there are conditions such that its non-existence follows from the non-existence of each one, like life and the absence of opposites relative to the existence of knowledge; or composite, meaning that several things are one condition for the conditioned. Fourth: The condition may be the locus of the judgment, and the cause is its attribute, meaning that the locus of the judgment may not be a cause for the judgment because it does not affect, rather what affects is the attribute of that locus which is the cause, as you have learned; but the locus of the judgment is a condition for the judgment insofar as its existence depends on it. [Commentary:] His saying: (the condition) i.e. without mediation, so its division into multiple and composite becomes apparent, and it is not valid that the parts of the composite are also conditions, making it multiple. His saying: (as you have learned that the cause is an attribute that necessitates a judgment for its locus). His saying: (it is a condition for the judgment etc.) i.e. insofar as the existence of the cause depends on it, and that is when the cause is inherent in the locus of the judgment, and whatever is a condition for the existence of the cause is a condition for the judgment, and it may not be a condition for the judgment based on the permissibility of the cause being external to the locus of the judgment; he restricted it with 'insofar as' because it is impossible for the judgment to depend on it apart from this respect, due to the impossibility of the effect depending on a condition. His saying: (or composite) the difference between it and the multiple—even though what depends on the composite depends on each of its parts, so that upon which it depends also becomes multiple here—is that the dependence here is essentially on the whole, and dependence on the parts is by mediation, and this is not the case in the multiple; also, the composite is a single essence, and this is not the case with the multiple mentioned. His saying: (because it does not affect) not because a single thing cannot be both receptive and active, but because it is necessary that the attribute of being knowing is not caused by other than knowledge, and it is not a locus for it.

Checkpoint
What is the key difference between multiple and composite conditions according to the passage?
A) Multiple conditions are always existent; composite can be non-existent.
B) In multiple, dependence is directly on each condition; in composite, dependence is directly on the whole.
C) Multiple conditions are for different conditioned things; composite is for one.
D) There is no real difference.

Key Takeaway
Multiple conditions are independent; a composite condition is a single condition made of parts that are conditions indirectly.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you examine your own beliefs about what is necessary for salvation, do you treat them as multiple independent conditions or as a single composite condition? How does this distinction affect your view of Allah's mercy?
?
Think of an area in your life where you rely on multiple factors to achieve something. Have you ever confused a composite condition for multiple independent ones, leading to a logical error in your planning or trust in Allah? How can you correct that?
?
This lesson refines how we think about conditions. Are there conditions in your faith that you treat as independent when they are actually part of a composite whole? What would change if you saw them as a unified requirement from Allah?

Logic and Technical Terms

Condition as Locus of Judgment and the Role of Cause
Explains condition as locus and distinguishes cause as attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the locus of a judgment (mahall al-hukm) is a condition for the judgment, not a cause; the cause is an attribute of the locus.

Core Idea
The locus is a condition, not a cause; the attribute is the true cause.

In causal analysis, we must distinguish between the thing that receives a judgment (the locus) and the attribute that brings about the judgment. This passage explains why the locus cannot be the cause and demonstrates how it serves as a condition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on locus and cause
Read the Arabic text and translation focusing on the fourth point. Note the key statement: 'الشرط قد يكون محل الحكم، والعلة صفته'.
The author then explains why the locus is not a cause: it does not affect, the attribute affects.
2
Understand the commentary on conditionality
The commentary elaborates that the locus is a condition for the judgment insofar as the cause depends on the locus. If the cause is outside the locus, the conditionality may not hold.
The qualification 'without mediation' indicates the locus is directly a condition for the judgment.
3
Reflect on the deeper reason
The commentary ends with an argument: the locus cannot be the cause because a single thing cannot be both receptive (locus) and active (cause), and the attribute of being knowing is not caused by its locus.
This reinforces the distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يمتنع لا يمتنع أن يكون الشرط عدمياً كانتفاء أضداد العلم بالنسبة إلى وجوده، إذ لا معنى للشرط إلا ما يتوقف المشروط في وجوده عليه لا ما يؤثر في وجود المشروط، حتى أن يكون عدمياً. وذهب بعضهم إلى أن الشرط لا بد أن يكون وجودياً. Key Terms
محل الحكم (locus of judgment)
علة ('illa)
صفة (attribute)
شرط (shart)
توقف (dependence)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The locus of a judgment is the cause of that judgment.
Correction: The locus is only a condition; the cause is an attribute inherent in the locus.

Checkpoint
Why is the locus of judgment not a cause according to the passage?
A) Because the locus does not exist.
B) Because the locus does not affect; the attribute affects.
C) Because the cause must be external to the locus.
D) Because the locus is a condition that cannot be a cause.

Key Takeaway
The locus of judgment is a condition, not a cause; the cause is an attribute of the locus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own understanding of Allah's attributes, have you ever unconsciously treated Allah's essence as the cause of His attributes rather than as the locus? This lesson teaches that the locus is only a condition, not a cause. How does this shift your perspective on the relationship between Allah and His attributes, and how might that affect your worship?
?
Consider an area in your life where you have attributed success or failure to a mere condition (e.g., effort, environment) rather than to the true cause (Allah's decree). This lesson distinguishes condition from cause. Will you now consciously acknowledge Allah as the sole efficient cause while recognizing conditions as mere necessities?
?
The passage argues that a single thing cannot be both receptive and active regarding the same attribute. Reflect on a time you took credit for something that was actually a gift from Allah. How can this lesson help you humble yourself and attribute every good in your life to its true source?
